riots agrees with the military and civilian authorities on the suppression of the riots. The Indian government has accepted the commission's assessment. The commission includes Sir Shah Muhammad Sulaiman, Chief Justice of the High Court and a Muslim, and Pankridge, Deputy Chief Justice. Sir Sulaiman believed that the incidents before the second shooting did not necessitate such a degree of shooting. Pankridge, however, believed that it was necessary. The Indian government has accepted Pankridge's opinion but stated that the points raised by Sir Sulaiman will be carefully considered.

Sir Sulaiman believes that an armored car had knocked down and run over several people, causing the crowd to be very angry and attack it. Sir Sulaiman believes that without this brutal act, a major change would not have been triggered. Pankridge did not agree with Sir Sulaiman. The Indian government

has agreed to consult with the military authorities on the dangers of using armored vehicles to suppress civil unrest, raised by Sir Sulaiman.

US Senate Meeting 95

Convened Yesterday to Consider Naval Treaty

Opposition Attempts to Delay

Supporters Prevent Absences

▲ Associated Press, Washington, June 6: According to the latest news today, President Hoover intends to submit his opinion on the London Naval Treaty to the Senate today, regardless of whether there is a quorum. Senator Watson claimed that he intended to send Senate guards to search for senators who

avoided attending the special Senate meeting, and those who still resisted would be arrested. This statement is shocking because the United States has never had such a precedent. According to the declaration of Senator Allen, the center of opposition to the London Treaty is concentrated among naval

opposition personnel in various countries. The trend of this treaty will prevent the naval tonnage of the UK and Japan from being increased, while the United States will have the advantage of building as much as possible within its comparative capacity.

Associated Press, Washington, June 6: It is said that supporters of the London Naval Treaty are now plotting to put the treaty to a vote within ten days. Opponents are trying to delay, believing that delay is beneficial to them and the longer the delay, the more opponents of the treaty there will be. It is said that if there is a lack of a quorum when the vote is reached, the supporters of the treaty intend to find ways to force the senators to attend the meeting. At the same time, the government authorities are also making every effort to lobby the Senate, and President Hoover is paying special attention to this matter, hoping that the treaty will be approved as soon as possible.

Japanese National Defence Plan

Four Giants Meeting Yields No Results 101

Dentsu, Tokyo, July 7: The naval four giants meeting consisting of the Minister of Finance, the Minister of Navy Taniguchi, the Chief of Naval Operations Okada, and the former Minister of Navy Kato, continued after the day before and convened again yesterday morning at 10:00 at the Minister of Navy's official residence in Kasumigaseki to discuss the new national defence plan and the Japanese policy for the upcoming disarmament conference in 1935. Former Minister Kato argued that replacing 8-inch gun cruisers with 6-inch gun cruisers creates a huge shortfall in force, and that submarines and aircraft have completely different capabilities, so using aircraft to make up for the lack of submarines is unreasonable, and the economic cost of using aircraft as a substitute is also very high. He forcefully attacked from the standpoint of military operations, focusing on two points, and finally strongly stated that when the marshal's conference consults the advisory officials' conference on the issue of military strength, the military will respond that the military

The force amount in the London Treaty Three-Country Agreement has real shortcomings for Japan. General Okada rose to mediate, saying that if the amount of military force is deemed insufficient, the result would be a denial of the London Treaty itself, which is very regrettable for Japan's national defence. At this time, a supplementary proposal can be admitted, and efforts should be made to implement the three major principles in the next parliament. But former Minister Kato still disagreed, and even though Finance Minister Taniguchi explained, he still did not agree. The meeting broke up unhappily at 2:30 p.m., and a third meeting was scheduled for today.

Large-Scale Domestic Match Company Emerges 103

Initiated by Liu Hongsheng and Others

Liu Hongsheng, chairman of the Jiangsu Match United Association, and others have initiated the organization of a large-scale domestic match company to resist the Swedish Match, known as the world's match king. The plan is to merge the existing "Shanghai", "Zhonghua" and "Yingchang" companies, gather the strength of the three companies to deal with the foreign Swedish Match. Among the three companies, Yingchang Company is the largest in scale, with three branch factories, one in Pudong, Shanghai, Zhenjiang, etc. The second is Zhonghua, with two factories, and the third is Suzhou Hongsheng Factory. After the merger of the three factories, the capital will be 3 million yuan. The amount of shares will be proportional to the size of the factory. It is also planned to establish a large China Match Shares Preparatory Office at 38 Ai Duo Ya Road in Shanghai. Mr. Liu Hongsheng is the director of the preparatory office. For more than ten days, he has been actively preparing, and everything is almost ready. It has been submitted to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for registration and will officially open soon. After the merger of the three companies, the wholesale headquarters will be established in Shanghai, and it is planned to establish a distribution office in Suzhou. Distribution offices must also be established in other places such as Nanjing and Zhenjiang to promote sales. As for the manufacturing factories, the existing factories will be used without setting up new factories, or the names of the factories will not be changed, and the trademarks will also not be changed. Only the three words "Great China" will be added, such as "Great China Hongsheng Factory" or "Great China Yingchang Factory" to identify them and facilitate the evaluation of improved products.

Appeal of Cotton Merchants for Inspection 104

Continuing to Submit to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to Reform Bad Practices

The Shanghai China Cotton Industry Association continued to submit to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce yesterday, requesting a thorough reform of cotton inspection and detailing that cotton merchants did not actually misunderstand or have other intentions. The text read: Submitting to the thorough cotton inspection previously submitted, the association did not misunderstand, and how dare it have other intentions. I believe that improving cotton production is not the responsibility of your ministry, and the purpose of cotton inspection is to eliminate the addition of water and

impurities. May I ask, who is actually doing the adding of water and impurities? Since your ministry established inspection bureaus in Hankou, Ningbo, and other places, has it been discovered that vendors are adding water and impurities in commodity distribution locations? In fact, this is done by a small number of bad elements, small vendors, and farmers. To eradicate the disadvantages, it is definitely not the responsibility of the vendors. In that case, commodity distribution locations have nothing to do with inspection, and what is the value of having an inspection bureau? If it is said to improve international trade, then from the fundamental point of view, it is possible to start inspecting goods that are sold overseas. Cotton merchants are not resolutely opposed to the government implementing inspections, but because of the layers of exploitation, the pain is too deep, almost to the point of being unable to do business, so they have to be bold and state clearly. I hope that the late Premier gave top priority to people's livelihood, and that your ministry also sympathizes with the difficulties of merchants. Since the opening of inspection bureaus in various places, what is the actual performance? It is difficult to hide from people's eyes. And if the cotton merchants are not deeply pained, how dare they make a sound of groaning without disease? As for the Shanghai Bureau Cotton Industry Consultant Meeting on September 10 last year, various local draft mimeographs were distributed on the spot. At that time, the consultants debated, and there was no result. The discussion also included how much natural moisture is contained, which should be resolved first, and then a reduction method should be determined. The director and the director did not have a correct answer. How would I know that the case was being discussed, and one party had not yet made a decision, and the other party had already submitted it to the department for approval, and the reduction method was announced and implemented. The so-called Cotton Merchant Consultant Meeting, the truth is almost like this. Your ministry has clear vision, I pray that you will calm down and examine the facts, reform all the bad practices of the cotton inspection office, so that the merchants will be relieved of their difficulties, and it will be very fortunate.

Foreign Merchants Reduce Freight Rates - British merchants Taikoo, Jardine, etc., foreign merchant vessels, in order to attract the export of staple goods to the Northern Ocean, took advantage of the fact that Tianjin can now be unloaded and Chinese vessels are not operating, and decided to reduce freight rates to attract passengers and goods. JISHENG HUI'S YIXING DISASTER RELIEF REPORT 109

The Chinese Jisheng Hui, according to a report from Director Zhang Junzhongkuan in Yixing, who is in charge of disaster relief efforts, has listed the following: (1) Disaster Situation: Yixing experienced a flood in the 17th year [of the Republic, i.e., 1928], followed by drought and locusts in the 18th year [i.e., 1929]. Wealthy individuals avoided bandits and relocated elsewhere, while the poor had no means of borrowing. The county has too many migrant residents. The main products are bamboo and pottery. Currently, due to fear of bandits, no outside merchants inquire about purchasing these goods. Large quantities of goods are stockpiled like mountains, and tens of thousands of workers are unemployed, unable to obtain even a meager bowl of porridge each day. This has led many to take the wrong path. The southeastern and southwestern mountainous areas are the most severely affected by the disaster. The entire county is divided into fourteen districts, with districts four, five, six, seven, eight, and nine being mountainous. Districts four, five, and six are in the southeast, while districts seven, eight, and nine are in the southwest. Our association is focusing on the southeastern three districts first. (2) Bandit Situation: The county borders Changxing in Zhejiang, as well as Jianping and Guangde in Anhui. Situated on the edge of Tai Lake, bandits can easily appear and disappear. Due to economic pressure, many have been driven to take risks and become bandits. (3) Relief Funds: Our association is jointly operating with the Jiangsu Provisional Relief Association, with the aim of rescuing those who cannot survive without relief. We are carefully verifying households to strictly prevent fraudulent claims. (4) Relief Friends: We have invited Sun Changhou, Shao Ganchen, Ge Yutang, Zhong Huichu, Wang Shiyuan, and other gentlemen to set off in five groups on June 28th to investigate households in the mountainous areas. (6) Difficulties in Investigation and Reporting: The disaster areas in the county are all adjacent to mountains and connected to Tai Lake. Banditry is rampant, and disaster-stricken households are scattered. Some mountainsides are dozens of li, or even eight or ten li and some two, three, four, five, six, seven, or eight li. Disaster-stricken households are grouped into small villages of one, two, three, four, seven, or eight families. The weather is hot, the roads are treacherous, and climbing is difficult. Military protection is ineffective due to the limited number of firearms. Increasing the number of firearms would be costly. We are in a dilemma. We have agreed with our relief friends to be frugal and cautious, not sparing personal sacrifice, to personally investigate and distribute aid to the best of our abilities in order to provide relief to the disaster-stricken people and to live up to the generous intention of the gentlemen of your association to provide disaster relief. It is heard that the association’s second batch of Yixing relief funds has already been remitted by Tongxin Zhuang in this city to Yixing’s Dingkang Run Zhuang and will be transferred to Director Zhang for distribution.

General Manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company

ZHAO TIEQIAO REPORTS ON THE COMPANY'S AFFAIRS 110

On the occasion of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's seventh anniversary on July 7th, General Manager Zhao reported on the company's affairs, saying: This reorganization of the company's internal structure has the following significance: (1) It aligns with economic principles; (2) It responds to the demands of the times; (3) It demonstrates the company's commitment to continuous improvement. When the company was first taken over, the previous methods were deemed unsuitable for reorganization. Reforms were added two years later, but they were not entirely satisfactory. Although the establishment of various departments and offices, as well as the consolidation of the business departments and the seemingly rash and disruptive splitting and merging of the Shanghai office, may appear superficially light and bothersome, they actually represent progress towards development, seeking a bright path for the company's future, which is no different from an automatic revolution. Therefore, based on the experience of reorganization over the past two years, a comprehensive reorganization is being carried out, based on economic principles and the requirements of the times. Since the beginning of the military unrest, the requisitioning of ships and the obstruction of freight transport have resulted in substantial tangible and intangible losses, making it necessary to reduce government expenditure and personnel. The dismissed personnel have not committed any misconduct, but their dismissal is due to budget constraints. In the future, when the company needs personnel, vacancies will be filled promptly. This reorganization is not limited to reducing government expenditure and personnel, but is based on the experience of reorganization over the past two years, combined with internal and external

shipping company systems, to carry out reforms aimed at increasing the efficiency of the company's colleagues. It starts with the management of the headquarters. It is now estimated that, from a passive perspective, savings in consumption can amount to more than 100,000 yuan per year. This

method can be extended to various branch offices, ships, machines, and affiliated institutions, and there will certainly be more to observe. At the same time, it is necessary to increase production from an active perspective, so the sum of one in and one out will certainly not be small. Over the past two years, I have known the abilities, knowledge, and experience of senior staff well. This time, the allocation of important responsibilities will certainly allow each to give full play to their strengths. The staff of each department will also be assigned duties by their respective department heads based on their abilities. Every move of the company is not only noticed by society, but also its appropriateness is closely related to the agricultural, industrial, and commercial interests of the entire country. It is hoped that colleagues will, from today onwards, pay attention to increasing

production and reducing consumption, and only then can they truly demonstrate their abilities, otherwise it will still be tantamount to self-disturbance. The organization and activities of various institutions are similar to machines. Assuming that power belongs to the government, like the power of a motor, I am the main belt of power transmission, the heads of each department are the branch belts of power transmission, and the staff of each department are the large and small wheels and the direct manufacturing machinery. In this way, each component can be considered sound and capable. From now on, we must always inspect each belt, each wheel, and each machine to see if there are any problems causing obstacles. Each department is responsible for its own duties and operates in an orderly manner, so the overall efficiency can naturally be improved. I am willing to encourage this with my colleagues.

HUANG BAIYING SHEDS TEARS OF SORROW IN COURT 112

Baiying Case Heard for the Second Time Yesterday Morning

Forty-odd Dance Hostesses Look Sleepy

Tong Sanmao's Testimony Highly Ridiculous

It has been nine days since dance hostess Huang Baiying was forced to take poison. During these nine days, the people of Shanghai who are concerned about this case have been eagerly awaiting its outcome. In particular, the topics discussed in dance halls are nothing more than Tong and Baiying. This is because dance hostesses have a sense of self-preservation, and every dance patron has a Baiying in their heart. Yesterday was the date for the second continuation of the trial. As many as five hundred spectators attended, with over a thousand eyes focused on this pitiful woman. As a result, every remark was heard attentively. When she described her loneliness and isolation, willing to sacrifice herself for others, sorrow arose from within, and tears streamed down her face. The entire audience was moved to sadness, while Tong Sanmao stood upright in the defendant's dock, uneasy. The judge asked a few questions, and his

witty answers caused laughter in the courtroom. The solemn atmosphere of the court seemed unable to restrain the sympathy for Baiying among the audience even in the slightest.

A TRUE PORTRAIT OF HUANG AND TONG'S ATTITUDES 113

Many women were in the audience, about forty dance hostesses, but most had tired faces, probably due to insufficient sleep and having to rise early to attend court. Huang Baiying's complexion was slightly better than before, and her spirit was quite lively. She wore an ocher-colored floral gauze shirt, with a white satin black-edged open-front vest. Her hair was draped behind her, parted on both sides, occasionally revealing a haggard and delicate appearance.

Tong Sanmao wore a white serge suit, with his shirt collar loose and no tie. His face was concave and his forehead prominent, with sunken eyes. He spoke very unnaturally, standing tall in the defendant's dock, attracting much attention. Some in the audience jeered and ridiculed him, especially when the judge questioned him. His answers, such as "She snatched the pills and wouldn't let me eat them" and "I was afraid she wouldn't eat them, so I insisted she eat them," caused laughter. Huang Baiying, on the other hand, had a face full of resentment and disdain.

EXTREMELY POTENT PILLS 114

The trial began at 8:45 a.m. yesterday. Judge Wu Tingqi and Prosecutor Guo Huaipu arrived in court and ordered the bailiffs to bring the defendant Tong Sanmao from the waiting room. First, Lawyer Li Zhishan, representing the police station, stood up and stated that the remaining sleeping pills taken by Huang Baiying had been sent by the police station to the health department for testing. The test results showed that the drug was extremely potent, with each tablet containing half a gram, equivalent to about seven and a half Chinese li. Taking one tablet can induce sleep, and the dose of seven tablets, or fifty li, can be fatal. Even less than seven tablets can be life-threatening and must be taken only on the advice of a doctor.

BAIYING'S EXPRESSION WHEN LEAVING THE COURT 115

DETAILED RECORD OF BAIYING'S TESTIMONY 116

Judge Wu then summoned Huang Baiying, who complied and stood at the witness stand, speaking fluent Mandarin. She stated that she was nineteen years old, a native of Guangdong, and resided in Shanghai's French Concession, Wanyi Lane, Luban Road. She worked as a dance hostess at the Paris Dance Hall on Jing'an Temple Road for over a year. She first met the defendant Tong Sanmao at the Datong Dance Hall around July or August of last year. Judge Wu then threw Huang Baiying's written record of her testimony at Baolong Hospital on June 30th to her for review, and asked if the record was accurate. He also asked if the words "Huang Baiying, twenty-nine" at the end of the record were her own handwriting. Huang examined it for a long time and then said that because she had taken poison at the time,

she was mentally confused, and it was difficult to remember whether she had signed the paper. She added that there were also inaccuracies in the record. Judge Wu then instructed her to describe the incident in detail. Huang said that on the night of the 29th of last month, after Tong finished dancing at the Paris Dance Hall, Mr. Fang Hengnian invited Tong and her to go out for a drive. She realized that Tong was going to make things difficult for her and tried to mediate. Unexpectedly, after getting into the car, Tong suddenly said to Fang, "You'll see in a week." At that time, the car was heading west. She did not pay attention to what Fang and Tong were saying in the car, so she did not know what they were saying. Later, when they drove to Beixinjing, the car stopped, and Tong and Fang both got out and talked. After a while, they got back in the car and drove back. At this time, Tong said to her in the car, "I have spent dozens of taels of silver to buy

a pistol, which I will use to shoot you." While speaking, he took out a bank passbook from his side and showed her the amount and date of the withdrawal. She was terrified at this moment. Tong then moved the seat cushion. Suspecting that something was amiss, she questioned him. Tong even

slapped her cheek. When the car reached Meibai Road, Mr. Fang said goodbye to them and got out of the car. Before leaving, Fang said to Tong, "Since you are friends with me, please do not make things difficult for Huang." After speaking, he turned away. Tong then instructed the driver to drive the car towards Wusong. Tong asked her in the car if she was willing to marry him. Because she was afraid, she shook her head repeatedly. Tong then asked her, "Can you or can't you?" She resolutely replied, "I can't." When the car drove to the bank of the Wusong River, Tong ordered the driver to get out of the car and then threatened her, saying, "This is where you will die. If you don't die now, then in the future, two people will have to die, or even three people will have to die." Huang Baiying burst into tears as she recounted this, but she still sobbed and continued to say that her parents had died early, "I am a lonely and weak woman. At that time, hearing Tong's words, I

decided to die to avoid harming others. I was about to throw myself into the river to commit suicide, but Tong stopped me again, saying that it was not good to die here. It would be better to take sleeping pills." He then ordered the driver to get back in the car and drive back, passing a place (i.e., the intersection of Huade Road and Zhaofeng Road). Tong then asked the driver to stop temporarily, and he got out of the car to buy medicine. After a while, he returned with a package of medicine and asked her for a yuan bill, then got out of the car again. Soon, he returned and ordered to drive straight to the gate of the Cangzhou Hotel on Jing'an Temple Road. Because she had not slept all night, she was tired at this time, so she asked Tong to help her out of the car and into the room of the hotel (room number 201). Tong asked the waiter to bring four bottles of soda and ordered paper and pens. After everything was ready, Tong closed the door and took out the medicine bottle, pouring the pills on the table. He first ordered her to write a letter, saying that she could write everything she wanted to say in the letter. She obeyed his orders, spread out the paper, dipped the brush in ink, and wrote a letter. The letter was addressed to Ma Shaozhen (Ma is also a dance hostess) at the Paris Hotel Dance Hall, and asked her to forward it to Zhang. Judge Wu asked who Zhang was, and Huang said that she did not want to reveal his name. When Tong saw that she had finished writing the letter, he used his palm to break open the soda bottles and ordered her to swallow the pills with the water. She swallowed them and moved closer to the window, hoping to meet someone familiar and ask for help. But Tong did not want her to stand for long and forced her to lie down. She refused, and Tong said, "If you don't sleep, you won't die." So she lay down. After a while, Tong asked her how she felt. She replied that she

felt nothing. Tong suddenly remembered that when he arrived at the hotel, he had written his real name in Western letters on the guest card. He was afraid that if she died, he would be implicated, so he asked her to move to Datong. She refused, and he hired a car to take her to Baolong Hospital. After treatment by the doctor, she woke up the next day. Soon, a detective from the police station came to the hospital to take her statement. Judge Wu then asked Huang Baiying a few questions. He asked, "Do you want to marry Zhang?" She replied, "Yes." He asked, "Are you engaged?" She replied, "No." He asked, "When did you tell Tong that you were going to marry Zhang?" She replied, "I didn't say it." He asked, "What kind of person is Zhang?" She replied, "He is studying at school." He asked, "Which school?" She replied, "I don't want to say because it involves his reputation." He asked, "Did you say to Tong Sanmao that you were willing to die?" She replied, "I didn't say it." He asked, "Did you say to Tong Sanmao, 'I am going to marry Zhang and I am sorry to you'?" She replied, "I didn't say it." He asked, "Did you bring the pills?" She replied, "He bought them." He asked, "Did anyone see you taking the pills?" She replied, "No one knew."

TONG SANMAO'S WITTY REMARKS 117

Judge Wu then summoned the defendant Tong Sanmao and instructed him, "Did you hear what Huang Baiying said today?" Tong replied, "I heard everything, but what she said is completely wrong." He asked, "Did you tell Huang about buying a gun in the car?" He replied, "I didn't tell her. After she took the poison, I wanted to take her to the hospital, but she didn't want to go. She also said that she had 400 yuan in cash at home and asked me to take it and escape." He asked, "Huang testified that in Wusong, you said to her that if Huang didn't die at that time, two people or even three people would have to die in the future. So, who were you trying to kill besides Huang? Was it Fang and Zhang?" He replied, "I didn't say that at the time. After returning from Song, I borrowed 30 yuan from a friend. Huang said that she had 12 yuan and that was enough. Huang then gave me one yuan to buy the pills, which cost 90 cents. After arriving at the Cangzhou Hotel and closing the room, I poured out the pills, intending to die together." He asked, "Since you wanted to die together, why didn't you take them first and force Huang to take them?" He replied, "I was afraid she wouldn't take them." He asked, "Then you should have swallowed them with her." He replied, "Huang had already swallowed all the pills, and there were none left for me to swallow." The audience then burst into laughter, and many privately discussed that Tong's words were witty, but Judge Wu had already realized that Tong was indeed a cunning person, so he stopped questioning him.

ADJOURNED HEARING FOR FURTHER EXAMINATION OF EVIDENCE 118

The witness Rong Kai, a Cantonese employee of the Cangzhou Hotel, was summoned and questioned about the situation of Tong and Huang at the hotel. According to Rong, the two people came to open a room and left after only a quarter of an hour. The hotel waiter Li Houshan and the driver Shi Jiake also described what they saw. Fang Hengnian was also summoned and asked if he had seen Tong show Huang the passbook and if Tong had mentioned buying a gun. Fang said that he only saw Tong show Huang a book, and he did not know about the gun. Fang also repeated what he had said in court before. The lawyers for both sides also cross-examined each witness one by one. Judge Wu then instructed the defendant Tong Sanmao to be detained and adjourned the hearing to 8:00 a.m. on July 16th.

PROSECUTOR JIN HENIAN APPEALS THE LU GENRONG CASE 119

Suzhou Quick News: In the case of the master-servant love affair between Huang and Lu, Lu Genrong, after the Higher Court concluded its second retrial and pronounced him not guilty, the original prosecutor, dissatisfied, filed an appeal. According to the initial judgment of the Lu District Court, the sentence was only two years. If there was no appeal, he could have been released after serving his time (the number of days of detention that have not been confirmed is usually counted as two days for one day). However, due to the appeal, the process was delayed, making it difficult for him to be released from prison. Now that an appeal has been filed, the Supreme Court will receive the notice, respond to the arguments, make a judgment, etc., which will inevitably require a certain period of time. A copy of the prosecutor's reasons for appeal was sent to Genrong by the Higher Court yesterday (the 7th). The full text is recorded as follows:

Notification Letter: Jiangsu Higher Court Notification Letter No. In the case of Lu Genrong from Wuxian helping with theft, the judgment was delivered on July 4th, 1920 [actually, the 19th year of the Republic, which is 1930]. The prosecutor has been granted permission to appeal the judgment of this court and has submitted an appeal brief stating the reasons for the appeal. A copy of the brief is hereby sent for your information. You must submit a response brief to this court in July, in accordance with Article 396, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Procedure Law, and attach a copy to be forwarded. This notice is hereby given. Right notice to Lu Genrong for information. A copy of the appeal brief is enclosed. July 7, 1930 [19th year of the Republic] Reasons for Appeal: Defendant Lu Genrong. The above defendant was declared not guilty by the Criminal Division of this court on June 30th of this year in the theft case. The prosecutor believes that an appeal should be filed and hereby presents the reasons as follows: The intent of the retrial in this case is twofold: first, whether Lu Genrong helped Huang Huiru commit theft before the act of theft was completed; and second, whether Lu Genrong transported the stolen goods after the act of theft was completed by Huang Huiru. After reviewing the entire file, although it cannot be proven how the defendant Lu Genrong helped Huang Huiru commit theft at the time of the theft, he cannot escape responsibility for transporting the stolen goods. The criminal act and criminal intent are discussed separately below: (A) Whether the defendant committed a criminal

Page 16

act: According to Huang Huiru's testimony in the first instance, "The things were taken out in the afternoon of the 12th. Lu Genrong came out on the 12th," etc. It is clear that the stolen goods obtained by Huang Huiru were transported out by the defendant. Huang Huiru's testimony has been consistently exonerating the defendant. For example, Lu Genrong admitted during the investigation that he hired a car to pick her up, while Huang Huiru testified during the trial that the car was hired by Ama, etc. Only on this point did she inadvertently reveal the truth, which is the key evidence in this case. Moreover, during the investigation, when the prosecutor asked, "When your mother checked on the 12th, the jewelry box was already gone?" Huang Huiru testified, "He beat me because I said the jewelry box was gone," etc. It is clear that on the 12th, Huang Zhu's searched for the jewelry box and, finding it missing, severely reprimanded Huiru, which is consistent with Huang Huiru's statement that the things were taken out in the afternoon of the 12th, etc. The defendant Lu Genrong also admitted to the Public Security Bureau that "I took Miss Huang Huiru out with me and took away valuable ornaments." Comparing and cross-referencing this initial testimony with Huang Huiru's testimony above, it is undeniable that he implemented the transportation. Regarding his statement "and took away valuable ornaments," it is clear that the word "I" in Lu Genrong's statement is from himself. The original judgment said that it referred to Huang Huiru. According to the original testimony, the tone is obviously inconsistent. (B) Whether the defendant had criminal intent is discussed separately below. (1) Lu Genrong had a wife, which is an undisputed fact. His seduction of Huiru was not intended to lead to marriage. This alone is enough to prove that adultery was only for the purpose of obtaining wealth, which was his goal and the cause of the crime in this case. (2) Lu Genrong had Huang Huiru send the aforementioned Huiru to secretly transport the leather box out the day before the escape, which cannot be excused as unintentional. Considering that the things were transported out first on the 12th and then a car was hired to pick up people on the 13th, etc., when the prosecutor asked during the investigation where (one character missing in the original text) they met on the 13th, Lu Genrong replied, "I hired a car to pick her up." It is undeniable that they colluded with each other. Moreover, according to the defendant's statement at the Public Security Bureau that he took away valuable ornaments, he not only knew that there were ornaments hidden in the box, but also that they were valuable. Lu Genrong had been working as a tea servant at Huang Zhu's house for a long time and knew that Huiru was still unmarried and that her mother managed the family property. Suddenly, when they agreed to escape together, he had her transport the valuable ornaments out in advance, which shows that he was absconding with the property, and it cannot be said that he was unaware. (3) After Huang Huiru was seduced by Lu, they became completely corrupt, like a couple. Later, they moved back and forth between Suzhou and Shanghai, changing their residence frequently and spending the ornaments together. How could they not know the origin of these ornaments? By drawing an inference, it is possible to obtain a conviction. The original judgment did not thoroughly study the above points, which is not enough to form a conviction. In summary, the original judgment declaring the defendant not guilty is not appropriate. Therefore, an appeal is filed and it is requested that the original judgment be revoked and a sentence be imposed in accordance with Article 376, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Law. To the Supreme Court. Inspector Jin Henian of the Jiangsu Higher Court. July 6, 1930 [19th year of the Republic]

Another Madman Murders 120

Lu Qiutao from Pusong District

Injures and Kills Multiple Men and Women

Lu Jinhua, a former resident of the West Market of Pusong Town, had four sons. The third son, Lu Qiutao, is forty years old. He has worked as a firewood carrier for many years. He is usually thrifty and his business is quite decent. Several years ago, he and his brothers built a large building, making them a moderately well-off family in the town. Unexpectedly, two years ago, Qiutao suffered some kind of mental shock and suddenly went insane. At first, he was still calm, but he stopped working and spent his days wandering the streets, muttering to himself, holding a donation register. He would talk about gods and Buddhas to acquaintances, asking them to solicit donations from the townspeople to build temples. Occasionally, he would become violent, and his family would chain him up for a few days, after which he would return to normal and resume his business as usual. However, he would relapse soon after. Last year, in February or March, when his madness struck, he would stay up all night, either scaring people like a ghost, or setting fire to fields where coffins were temporarily stored, or even setting fire to his own house or other people's houses. Fortunately, he was always seen in time, and no major disasters occurred. This time, he actually committed a major case of injuring and killing multiple people. The details are as follows:

Destroying His Own Doors and Windows The Lu Qiutao household includes his brother, sister-in-law,

nephews, and nieces, as well as a wife and two daughters. They formed a small family, renting a house and

running a small grocery store. Before 4 PM on the sixth of this month, he was still working, selling rice straw to customers, showing no signs of madness. Unexpectedly, he suddenly went insane, holding a white-eye birdcage, slowly walking from the west of the store to his home. Upstairs, he smashed the doors, windows, and furniture in his house, yelling loudly. His brother and sister-in-law heard the commotion and, knowing that he was causing trouble, took sticks and other weapons to subdue him. Seeing this, the madman ran downstairs, grabbed a kitchen knife, and went out the door, still holding the birdcage, heading east. His brother and sister-in-law did not know he had a knife and paid little attention, not pursuing him, unaware that he was about to kill people.

Attacking a Mother and Son at a Blacksmith Shop The thatched cottage was a blacksmith shop owned by Ni Binggao. At the time, the entire Ni family was having dinner under the shed in front of the house. They saw Lu, holding a birdcage and walking quickly, not suspecting madness, paying no attention. Unexpectedly, as he approached, he took out the kitchen knife and slashed at the shop owner's wife's head, causing her to fall to the ground, bleeding profusely. The shop owner, Ni Binggao, and others all ran away in fear. However, his four-year-old son, unable to escape, was slashed four times, once on the eyebrow, once on the chest, and twice on the back, immediately falling to the ground.

Killing People Along the Way After injuring the mother and son at the blacksmith shop, the madman strode eastward, killing anyone he saw along the way. A bamboo shop owner named Xu, who lived nearby, ran wildly in front of the madman, shouting, "Lu Qiutao, the madman, is coming to kill people!" At this time, everyone was having dinner, and hearing the cries, they all fled in terror. The sound of footsteps and screams rose up, like a raging horse and crashing waves. The madman walked east to a noodle shop, where he encountered a country boy in his teens returning from the market with groceries. The madman slashed at him with the knife. The boy, terrified, fell. Fortunately, it was near the Xuehua River bank, and he fell and rolled down to the bank, avoiding injury.

Then Kills the Shop Owner and a Customer A lane to the east of the noodle shop

was the Shen Hengxing teahouse and grocery store. The shop owner, Shen Zi- , was handing money to a customer when the madman broke in from behind, taking him by surprise, and slashed at his neck. The shop owner, fearing his madness, did not resist and fled in pain. The madman wandered away, still holding the birdcage in his hand. He walked east to the Li Wanhe wine shop, where a man named Zhu was leaning against the counter, drinking wine and chatting with the shop assistant, enjoying himself. The madman lightly tapped Zhu's neck a few times with the back of the knife. Zhu looked back, not thinking he was crazy, paying no attention. The madman left, but after only a few dozen steps, he suddenly turned around and rushed at Zhu with the knife. Zhu, seeing the danger, reached out and grabbed the madman's wrist, holding it firmly, while shouting for help. The shop assistant and neighbors, seeing the situation was bad, rushed forward and snatched the knife from the madman. The knife was taken by a butcher named Yang. The madman then bit Yang hard on the back, injuring his skin and tearing his clothes.

The Murder Weapon is Seized and the Madman is Captured By this time, more and more neighbors were gathering.

The police also arrived. Although the madman's knife had been taken away, he was still very strong and punched and kicked, and those who were weak dared not approach. A police officer grabbed him from behind, but the madman bit off his little finger. A man named Wu was slapped in the face several times. Finally, a butcher's assistant named Li used all his strength and fighting skills to knock the madman down, and the police were able to hold him down on the ground, tie him up with rope, and carry him to the police station.

Muttering Nonsense Incessantly After the madman was detained at the First Precinct of the Sixth District, when Chief Wang interrogated him, he was still furious, glaring and muttering nonsense incessantly. He mostly refused to answer questions. When asked why he wanted to kill people, he replied, "I wanted to kill people myself. Now that you've put me here, I'm very happy and willing." He was completely unreasonable. Chief Wang, considering the matter involved a capital crime, sent him to the judicial section of the Municipal Public Security Bureau for further investigation.

The Injured are Sent to the Hospital for Treatment Besides a certain police officer and the butcher, the blacksmith's wife had a wound on her head that was more than an inch deep and seemed quite serious. The four-year-old son's four wounds were not deep and probably wouldn't be fatal. The tea shop owner, Shen Ziqing, had a neck wound that was more than three inches long, but it didn't reach the skull. All were sent by police car to the Chinese Red Cross Society Hospital in Jing'an Temple for treatment.

Post Office Truck Driver's Suspected Suicide Cannot Be Confirmed 121

Only the Disappearance Can Be Proven

Letter from China Merchants Bureau to Post Office

Regarding the disappearance of a truck driver surnamed Zhang from the Postal Administration, as reported earlier, some details have emerged. It is generally believed that he committed suicide by jumping into the sea. The information we have gathered is as follows:

Discovery of Jumping into the Sea The China Merchants Bureau's Xin Jiangtian轮 departed from Shanghai for Ningbo on July 2. A passenger was traveling to Ningbo. When the ship arrived in Zhenhai, the sky was still dim. The ship's steward discovered that a passenger was missing. After reporting to the purser, they went to the passenger's cabin and found two sets of clothes. After examination, they learned that it belonged to the truck driver who worked at the Shanghai Post Office. When the Xin Jiangtian returned to Shanghai, they sent the clothes to the post office for verification.

Clothes Sent for Confirmation After the ship returned to Shanghai, in addition to reporting to the General Bureau, the ship's purser sent two stewards with the missing driver's belongings to the post office to ask if they were his. At that time, the post office verified them and confirmed that they were indeed his. That was how they discovered he had disappeared. The post office then took the clothes.

Letter to the Bureau for Investigation Yesterday, the Postal Administration sent a letter to the China Merchants Bureau, asking if the crew of the Xin Jiangtian could confirm that the truck driver had indeed jumped into the sea and died. The China Merchants Bureau replied to the Post Office, generally based on the steward's report, only knowing that he had disappeared after arriving in Zhenhai. As for confirming that he jumped into the sea, since no one witnessed it, it was difficult to say for sure, and the reason was even more difficult to know.

A Widow Seduced by a Scoundrel Heartbroken and Commits Suicide by Drowning.

Yang Dongshan Cheats a Friend's Wife 123

Sells All Her Clothes and Runs Away 124

Then Dates a Rich Woman and Dresses Lavishly 125

The Widow is Grief-Stricken and Attempts Suicide but is Rescued 126

Yesterday morning around 10 AM, a young woman boarded ferry number 13 at the Customs Pier to cross the river. When the boat reached the middle of the river, the woman suddenly jumped into the river to commit suicide. Fortunately, the crew was quick and immediately rescued her, saving her life. The boatman Xu Maomao sent her to the Water Police Station. She said her name was Zhang Jinxian, 24 years old, from Changzhou. She married in her hometown at the age of 16. Soon after, her husband died of illness, leaving behind a five-year-old son. The widow and orphan found life very difficult. Her in-laws did not pity her for her widowhood. Two years ago, a friend of her late husband, Yang Dongshan, seduced her, claiming that it was not worth living such a lonely life at home, without any joy. He also said that he had bought a mahogany bed and other valuable furniture in Shanghai and was willing to live with her and grow old together, seeking the inherent happiness of life. She was temporarily deceived by his sweet words and took her son and the gold, silver, and clothes of considerable value from her home and ran away to Shanghai with Yang. When they arrived in Shanghai, the so-called mahogany bed turned out to be a broken bed made of three pieces of pine board. The other furnishings were also very simple. Being unfamiliar with the place and unable to call for help, she had no choice but to temporarily endure. They lived together for two years, but he had no regular job, and gradually all the gold, silver, and clothes she had brought were used up. They gradually had no food or clothing. She had no choice but to work as a servant in other people's homes. Seeing that she had no money to provide, Yang suddenly changed his kind and gentle face and accused her of having a new lover. Unable to argue effectively, he left on December 19th of last year and disappeared. She thought that when she had money, Yang was very affectionate, but when she had no money, he abandoned her as if she were trash. Such a conscienceless act was no different from the vicious tactics of a swindler. At that time, she temporarily moved to Gu Maolin's house at 127 Zhen'an Lane, Gonghe Road, Zhabei, and continued to work as a servant in the original place to make a living. Recently, she learned that Yang had a new rich woman and they were as close as glue, living in a small house somewhere. Yang's clothes were also extraordinarily luxurious, unlike his previous poor attire. She was heartbroken and increasingly depressed, leading to her feelings of world-weariness. She said, "The woman he's with will end up just like me when he spends all her money." She sobbed uncontrollably. The detective sympathized with her and advised her. He ordered the landlord Gu Maolin to be brought to the case and took her back.

A Daughter-in-Law is Fierce, and the Mother-in-Law Dies From Poison

The Daughter-in-Law Flees in Fear of Punishment 127

The Daughter Comes to Shanghai to Collect the Body 128

The elderly woman Chen Chen, 59 years old, had a son who married a daughter-in-law. The daughter-in-law was exceptionally fierce. On the first of this month, the daughter-in-law had a major argument with Chen Chen over a trivial matter. Chen Chen angrily took poison. After her neighbors realized what had happened, they sent her to Tongren Hospital, then transferred her to Guangren Hospital. She recently died. Her son and daughter-in-law heard the news and fled in fear of punishment. The hospital notified the Harbin police, who sent detectives to move the body to the Pei Lun Road morgue. Yesterday morning, the Special District Court appointed Prosecutor Guo to the morgue to examine the body. According to the Western Deputy Detective, Luo Chen, who identified herself as the daughter of the deceased, said, "The deceased is my mother. I lived with my husband in Suzhou. After learning that my mother had taken poison, I rushed to Shanghai to see her, but she was already unable to speak. Now I will claim the body." Prosecutor Guo reviewed the testimony and said, "It is determined that the deceased female corpse, Chen Chen, died from opium poisoning. The corpse is handed over to the daughter, Luo Chen, to claim and bury."

Two Criminals Share a Car, Nose Broken, Arm Fractured, Leg Shattered

A Tram Smashes Into a Rickshaw

The Rickshaw Puller's Leg is Also Broken

The Haiyun Customs Brokerage firm sent a cargo ship loaded with broadcloth to the Qinhuangdao Road pier the other day to unload goods onto the Pinglong丸 vessel. Unexpectedly, four or five bandits, including Zhang A'er and Zhang Liangying, holding knives and axes, broke into the ship, threatened the sailors, and stole a box of broadcloth. The Customs Brokerage firm reported it to the Weituoma Road Water Police Station, who sent detectives Wang Haiquan and others to arrest Zhang A'er and Zhang Liangying. After a clear interrogation, at 10 AM yesterday, the detective was ordered to escort the two criminals to the District Court. The two criminals, handcuffed together, were sitting in a rickshaw. While traveling on the tracks on Chezhan Road in front of the District Court, a China Merchants Route 4 tram, traveling north, rang its bell to warn them, but the rickshaw puller ignored it, so the tram could not avoid hitting the rickshaw from behind. The rickshaw was smashed, and the rickshaw puller's leg was broken. Zhang A'er and Zhang Liangying were thrown from the car, their noses were broken, their arms fractured, and their legs shattered, all suffering serious injuries. The police arrived, recorded the tram as number 26 and the driver as number 81, and took the injured rickshaw puller to the Second District Police Station, ordering driver number 81 to report to the station. Zhang and the other criminal were first sent to the court for interrogation and detention, and then sent to the hospital for treatment.

Public Works Bureau Restricts Rowing Boat Licenses 129

The Municipal Public Works Bureau believes that rowing boats are of simple construction and can only travel on inland rivers. If they are on the Huangpu River, carrying passengers is often dangerous, and they cannot carry heavy loads. As they are without a fixed business and because the cost is very low, many unemployed and homeless people use them to engage in illegal activities, which has long been criticized by travelers on the Huangpu River, especially for transporting contraband, which endangers public security. The bureau's intention in registering, inspecting, and issuing licenses for these rowing boats is to gradually eliminate them. Therefore, it has consulted with the Finance Bureau to exempt them from taxes. The total number of registered rowing boats has reached 1,308. If restrictions are not imposed, they will continue to increase sharply, which will defeat the purpose of the ban. The 138th bureau meeting decided to stop registering rowing boats. From July onwards, only transfers and returns of licenses will be allowed, and no new licenses will be issued, to show restriction. The Municipal Government has approved this method.

News from the Red Cross Epidemic Hospital 130

Opening Set for the 10th

The Chinese Red Cross Society's Epidemic Hospital on Tianjin Road has been properly arranged. Although the buildings are old, they have been greatly repaired this year and have been completely renovated. The official opening is set for the 10th of this month. During the repair period, Dr. Wang Peiyuan, the president and medical director of the association, ordered doctors Zhou Hongzhang, Wang Zhenchuan, Zhang Danqing, and head nurse Li Naishuang to be stationed at the hospital to prepare for the opening and to diagnose and treat summer illnesses and administer vaccinations in advance. In the past ten days, there have been more than 300 cases. With the hot and humid weather in recent days, the number of patients coming to the hospital has increased, keeping doctors Zhou Hongzhang and others very busy.

Ningbo Native Association Runs a Free Clinic 132

The Ningbo Native Association in Shanghai is a group of Ningbo people in Shanghai. They are enthusiastic about starting charitable and public welfare matters on weekdays. Considering the large number of Ningbo natives in Shanghai, most of whom are poor, and once they get sick, it is difficult for them to see a doctor due to financial reasons, the 11th Executive Committee of the association decided to run a free clinic within the association to provide relief. It is reported that registered national doctors Jiang Zhuqing, Zhuang Yu, and Yu Daowei have been invited as medical directors, so that poor and sick fellow villagers who cannot afford medical treatment can receive free treatment. It is scheduled to start providing free treatment from the 16th of this month, and it is stipulated that the free treatment time will be from 10 AM to 3 PM every day.

A Dispute Over a Towel at a Public Swimming Pool 133

Russian Detective Accuses Someone of Theft

Wang Caiqi is Imprisoned

The other day at dusk, there were Chinese and Western people bathing in the public swimming pool on Jiangwan Road. After bathing, Wang Caiqi, a Pudong native among the bathers, wiped his face with a large towel that belonged to a Russian named Qiulun in the neighboring room. Qiulun, who is a detective in the General Patrol Room, saw Wang taking his towel without permission and thought it was theft. He wanted to take him to the patrol room. When he was about to leave, Guan Bomin, an Anhui native also bathing there, thought it was a misunderstanding and that the Russian should not make a fuss over a small matter, so he stopped the Russian from performing his duties. As a result, there was a conflict between the two parties, and more and more onlookers gathered. Qiulun called the police, who took Wang and Guan, along with the towel, to the patrol room. Yesterday morning, they were taken to the Special District Court by Judge Feng Shide for trial. Qiulun testified that Wang stole his towel and was caught. Instead, he was robbed by Guan and others and wanted to be beaten. Wang Caiqi said that it was actually a misunderstanding and that he had been beaten by the Russian. Guan Bomin testified that he was only trying to dissuade them and was also punched and kicked by the Russian, who pointed a gun at him and called him a Communist. However, several Westerners who testified for Qiulun said that Qiulun did not hold a gun or beat anyone. Judge Feng said that the testimonies differed. He ordered Wang to be detained, Guan to pay 500 yuan bail, and asked for additional witnesses for another hearing.

Examination of a Person Who Died in Bed 134

Yang Yongyu Died of Acute Cholera

Yang Yongyu, a native of Zhenjiang, went to his sister's house at 5 Lianzhili, Baoshan Road, to avoid mosquitoes in his house in Gaochang Temple. His sister and his wife went to the playground to play. When they returned home, Yang was stiff on the bed. The situation was reported in yesterday's newspaper. Yesterday, Prosecutor Li and Inspector Shen arrived on the scene. It was determined that the deceased had died of acute epidemic cholera. His wife and sister were not by his side at the time, and no one took care of him, so he died in vain.

The Eldest Daughter Commits Suicide by Drinking Raw Opium Because She is Sad About Her Lack of Freedom in Marriage 135

Lu A'e, a woman from Shaoxing, 19 years old, with a slight appearance, has been an eldest daughter in the Bao family at 15 Jiani Lane, Avenue Edward VII, for five or six years. A few days ago, her mother in her hometown betrothed her to a small husband who was only 14 years old. She wrote a letter to her about it. Lu was very upset after hearing the news. She had been living in Shanghai for a long time, and she had heard and seen that men and women had absolute freedom in marriage. She did not want to marry this rural child. She suddenly became depressed. Although the employer tried to persuade her gently, A'e was still concerned about it, thinking that there was no hope for her lifelong happiness. At 10:30 AM yesterday, she secretly drank raw opium and committed suicide. The employer noticed it and accompanied her to Renji Hospital for treatment. However, she died around 5 PM that afternoon due to an overdose of poison.

A Husband and Wife Officially Married Stay Overnight at an Inn 136

Hu Ayou and Wu

Hu Ayou, a Ningbo native living at 38 Zhongyu Lane, Yongxing Road, Zhabei, who used to be a painter, went to the Ning'an Hotel at the end of North Zhejiang Road (Chinese Concession) with a young girl named Wu the night before last, and opened a room to stay overnight. Around 1:00 AM that night, the patrol chief of the First Precinct of the Fourth District went to the hotel to check on the guests. Seeing that Hu looked suspicious, he immediately took him to the precinct. Chief Yao interrogated Hu Ayou, who said he was 24 years old and Wu was his wife, whom he had married for many years. Wu said that she had married Hu last year. Chief Yao checked the records and, because their testimonies did not match, ordered them to be detained. Yesterday morning, a police officer was sent to the landlord at 38 Zhongyu Lane, Yongxing Road, to prove that Hu and Wu were officially married. They were then released, but they had been sitting in the police station all night, suffering a false alarm.

Lu Wei Commits Suicide 137

As a Result of Arguments and Beatings by Lu Yueder

Lu Yueder, a native of Funing, Jiangbei, living at 57 Tianbao Road, Hujia Muqiao, Shanghai North, has been working as a rickshaw puller and has been married to Wei (also a native of Funing, currently 38 years old) for many years. Lu is short-tempered and disputes often arise between husband and wife. The day before yesterday, he argued with Wei over a trivial matter, and then grabbed Wei and beat her. Wei became angry and developed a feeling of world-weariness. That night, she took off her belt and hanged herself in the room. By the time Lu realized it, she was already cold as ice, and there was no way to revive her. He immediately reported it to the Third Precinct of the Fifth District, who ordered a guarantor to report it to the District Court. Yesterday afternoon, a prosecutor was sent to the scene to determine that the husband was ordered to prepare a coffin for burial pending verification.

Discord Between Mother-in-Law and Daughter-in-Law Almost Led to Tragedy 138

Song Zhou Attempts Suicide by Hanging and is Rescued

Song Caijin, a Ningbo native, 35 years old, rented a house at 35 Zhuhang Lane, Nanshi. Ten years ago, he married a Zhou woman from the same hometown through a matchmaker. Zhou is now 27 years old. After she passed through the door, the couple suddenly had different opinions, and their relationship deteriorated day by day. His aunt, Wang, 61 years old this year, is violent. Neighbors call her a tigress. She often disliked that Zhou had been married for many years and had not yet given birth, so she often abused her. Zhou could not bear the pain, but because she respected her mother-in-law, she could do nothing but complain to herself. Unexpectedly, yesterday, Wang started a quarrel with her daughter-in-law Zhou over a trivial matter and beat her again, saying that it would be better for her to die sooner. Zhou was extremely angry and resentful after hearing this bad remark. She secretly went into the bedroom, took off her belt and hanged herself. Fortunately, she was discovered in time and rescued. The neighbors heard about it and were indignant. They immediately reported it to Zhu Xuanliang, the sentinel of the Eighth Guard Post there, who took Song Wang and her son to the General Bureau of the First District, where they were ordered to be temporarily detained pending a preliminary hearing.

Transfer of Bandit Leader in Anhui Kidnapping Case 139

All Three Bandits Were Extremely Cruel

Even After Receiving Ransom, They Still Tore Up the Ticket

The three bandits from Anhui, He Debin (aka He Peilin), Hu Mingzhao, and Li Jingming, etc., kidnapped Zhan Jiapeng, the uncle of merchant Zhan Fugao from Rendefang, Dongcheng in their hometown of Guangde County, Anhui Province, during the twelfth lunar month of last year. They sent a letter to the victim's family, demanding a ransom of 200,000 [monetary units] for his release. The victim's family sent someone to negotiate with the bandits and agreed to pay a ransom of 8,000 [monetary units], with 4,000 [monetary units] paid upfront. Unexpectedly, after receiving the ransom, the bandits tore up the ticket and buried the body in the wilderness outside the western city, destroying the evidence. The local government issued an arrest warrant. The bandits then fled to Shanghai, hiding in a shoe store on Avenue Edward VII. The Guangde County government learned of their whereabouts and sent detectives Chen Yuankai, Jin Yongxin, and Zeng Ronghua to Shanghai with official documents. They reported to the French Concession Police, requesting assistance in arresting the suspects. Police Inspector Jin Jiulin and Detective Qian Yumin were dispatched to assist in locating the address. The three bandits were arrested and taken to the police station. Yesterday, they were brought to the French Concession Court for questioning. The visiting detectives presented the official documents, stating the case and requesting permission to extradite the three defendants for trial. He Debin, Hu Mingzhao, and Li Jingming confessed directly to the kidnapping of Zhan Jiapeng and tearing up the ticket after the ransom was not fully paid. Judge Zhu ruled that since the defendants had confessed, they should be handed over to the visiting detectives for trial in their original jurisdiction.

Shop Assistant Falsely Reports Robbery 140

Gambling Away Received Funds

Making Excuses to Evade Responsibility

Recently, the Hongkou Police Station has received several false reports of robberies. Upon investigation, it was found that the perpetrators were shop assistants who had collected payments and then gambled them away, unable to account for the missing funds. They resorted to this tactic to try to deceive their employers. Although detectives have investigated and sent those who made false reports to court for punishment, such incidents continue to occur. The police station is expending considerable effort on these cases. At 10 PM the night before last, a Ningbo native named Zhang Longhua reported to the police station, claiming that he was a runner for the Yongmao Hat Company in the French Concession. He had been ordered to collect payments from various merchants, amounting to over 30 [monetary units]. At 5 PM, while passing Taoyuanfang on North Jiangxi Road, he was suddenly accosted by two robbers. One robber brandished a gun, threatening him and taking all the money from his person. Therefore, he came to report the incident. The police chief found it suspicious that Zhang reported the robbery five hours after it occurred. He ordered Chinese Detective Sun Dehui and a Western detective to investigate the scene of the alleged robbery. They found no evidence of a robbery. They returned to the police station and detained Zhang. Under questioning, Zhang confessed that he had gambled away the collected funds and, unable to face his employer, had made a false report, asking for leniency. The police chief verified the confession and ordered him to be detained, awaiting transfer to the Special District Court for severe punishment to serve as a warning to others.

Future Motorcycle Racing Track 141

Construction Begins Today, Expected to Be Completed in Two Weeks

Opening Near the Willow Garden at the End of the Month

Overseas Chinese Riders Return Home to Showcase Their Skills

The World Motorcycle Association has held several races in Shanghai,

renting the Shenyuan grounds each time. The events have attracted a large number of spectators, with excellent results and successful outcomes. Now that the Shenyuan rental

contract has expired, concerned Chinese and Western individuals have specifically requested that the association stay in Shanghai for several months for a long-term performance. A permanent motorcycle racetrack is being built near the Willow Garden on Route de Zikawei in western Shanghai for racing purposes. Construction begins today, with completion expected in two weeks. The track will be approximately 400 yards long, with five laps equaling one mile. Grandstands will be built around the track, accommodating approximately 6,000 people. Furthermore, five renowned Chinese riders have been hired from Singapore to participate in the races. The opening is scheduled for the end of this month. The center of the track will be used as a soccer field for the recreational use of Chinese and foreign athletes.

Coroner's Examination of a Boy Killed by a Car 143

The mother of Zhang Miaolin, a villager from Pudong, who lived at 376 Avenue du Roi Albert in the French Concession, passed away on the 5th. Zhang received the news in the countryside and brought his six-year-old son, Zhang Fugen, to Shanghai for the funeral arrangements. That evening, the father and son were cooling off in front of their door. Fugen was running and playing in the road with neighboring children. At 8:45 PM, a car, license number 10258, driven by Huang Peilin, a chauffeur from a car company at 72 Guangxi Road, was traveling south and failed to avoid Fugen, hitting him. The police arrived and took both parties to the police station. The police chief ordered Huang to post bail and instructed that the injured child be sent to Renji Hospital for treatment. Due to the severity of the injuries, the child died before treatment could be administered. The hospital notified the police station, which transported the body to the Tongren Fuyuantang morgue for examination. Yesterday, the Vehicle Affairs Office summoned the family of the deceased and the defendant to the scene. Judge Zhu of the French Concession Court arrived to examine the body. After taking his seat, he questioned the defendant and then ruled that the deceased boy, Fugen, had died from injuries sustained after being hit by a car. The family of the deceased should prepare a coffin for burial, and the police station should take photos of the body for record-keeping, pending further review.

Four-Corner Numeral Indexing Training Institute 145

Opening Ceremony Held Yesterday

The Commercial Press established the Four-Corner Numeral Indexing Training Institute during this summer to train students from well-known secondary and higher schools nationwide as trainees. The plan is to use the Four-Corner Numeral Indexing method invented by Wang Yunwu to create indexes for various dictionaries and reference books published by the press. These indexes will be attached to the books to facilitate checking by people from all walks of life. The institute held its opening ceremony yesterday morning at 9 AM. Guests included Cai Yuanpei, Hu Shih, as well as Gao Mengdan, director of the Commercial Press; Li Bake, manager; Zhuang Baiyu, chief of confidential material; He Bocheng, director of the translation office; Li Bojia, head of the publishing department; and instructors Xu Baode, Chen Zixin, Mao Songgan, Fang Guifen, Zhao Jingyuan, Cao Yikong, and Zong Youze, along with more than 200 trainees. The ceremony was performed as scheduled. First, the chairman, He Bocheng, reported the purpose of the training institute. Then, Hu Shih, Cai Yuanpei, and Zhuang Baiyu gave speeches on the importance of indexing and the advantages and applications of the Four-Corner Numeral Indexing method. It was reported that the first class mainly consists of students recommended by schools in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, totaling 106 schools. Trainees selected by schools from distant provinces have been assigned to the second class. It is said that many schools are still enthusiastically sending recommendations to the institute in the coming days.

Letter to the Editor 149

To the Esteemed Editor of Shenbao,

Having read yesterday's report in your newspaper regarding the death of Mr. Cheng Pu's wife due to an abortion, the statement "the plaintiff, along with the deceased's nephew Cheng Yanqing and witness Lu Baofa, testified in court about the events" seems to be a misunderstanding. After investigating, the deceased had invited me for a consultation on June 11th. At that time, I saw that her condition was serious and believed that she needed to be admitted to a hospital. Therefore, at the patient's request, I introduced her to Dr. Bu at Dahu Hospital for treatment. The patient had not mentioned any abortion history to me before. I also had no knowledge of her condition after she went to Dahu Hospital. Therefore, when I was summoned to court for questioning, I only mentioned that the deceased had once invited me for a consultation and was not a witness to her death due to an abortion. Therefore, I am making this special statement, hoping to publish this letter in your newspaper to dispel any misunderstandings. Respectfully yours, Lu Baofa, July 7th.

Respectfully, it is now reported that Jingqin Textile Factory claims to have seen a news item in the Shenbao of July 6, "Textile Factory Suspected of Arson for Compensation," which is surprising. On the afternoon of June 29, approximately 6 PM, smoke was discovered in the factory. Cotton blankets and paper were found under a bed in the workers' dormitory. As the factory manager was away at the time, besides temporarily storing the discovered items in the accounting room, no action could be taken. The next day, after the manager returned to the factory, he investigated again and found nothing. He immediately reported the information to the Gaocang Temple Second District Police Station, which forwarded it to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation. It is not difficult to uncover the truth. This is the process. According to the news, the factory has three branch factories, and all have received compensation due to fires, which is entirely untrue. The factory has no branches, which can be investigated. Also, two fires within a year are not true. It is believed that this is a plot by malicious people. As the inaccurate information concerns the factory's reputation, we especially request your paper to allow our representative to notify the newspaper for correction. Respectfully to the Editor of Shenbao, Lawyer Wang Zhengqi, July 7th.

Social News

New Invention for Coloring Crystals 150

Utilizing X-rays

According to the Japanese News, Kato Toshio, assistant at the Physics Therapy Department of Keio University Hospital, has now completed the invention of artificially coloring crystals. Mr. Kato, 29, graduated from the Medical University two years ago and has been specializing in Roentgen therapy. Since last winter, he has been working at the Yamanashi Prefectural Hospital in Kofu. By taking colorless crystals from the prefecture and using the strong penetrating power of X-rays, he can achieve various colors and add more refined colors to natural colored crystals. According to him, he has now achieved great success in using X-ray radiation for 10 to 30 hours. Larger crystals up to three inches in diameter are also suitable, and he is currently researching further. Crystals from the Ural Mountains and the State of Bahia in Brazil are suitable for coloring, while crystals from Mt. Kinpu cannot be colored.

British Factories and Railways

Number of Deaths and Injuries 151

A Total of Over 5.6 Million Since the End of the War

More Than the Number of British Soldiers Killed and Wounded in the Great War

London News: According to official statistics, the number of people killed and injured in British factories and

railways during peacetime is more than the number of British soldiers killed in the Great War. The British army lost 1,089,099 soldiers and 2,400,988 wounded during the Great War, totaling 3,490,907. Since 1918, the number of deaths and injuries in factories is 27,919 and 4,144,721, totaling 4,172,631. The number of deaths and injuries on railways is 56,000 and 1,450,000, totaling 1,506,000. The total of the two items is 5,678,631, exceeding the total population of the Lancashire industrial area, which is alarming.

Soviet Russian Navy Regains Control of the Baltic Sea 152

Riga (Latvia) News: Since sending two warships to the Black Sea in May, the Soviet government has continued to arm itself rapidly in order to regain hegemony in the Baltic Sea. The 26,000-ton dreadnought "Frunze" being built in Petrograd, with all its equipment being new, has 12 large guns and has recently been completed. Construction has also begun on four 900-ton submarines, costing 14 million [monetary units] in silver dollars. The Soviet Navy now controls the Baltic Sea again. Its naval strength includes three 26,000-ton dreadnoughts with a total of 36 guns, one cruiser (Aurora), 32 destroyers, and 10 submarines. Its fighting power exceeds the total strength of the warships of all Baltic Sea countries. Soviet naval officials claim that the Red Fleet can prevent any powerful nation's fleet from invading the Baltic Sea through the Danish straits when necessary.

Japanese Trade with China Gradually Returns to Normal

Cargo Loaded on Japanese Ships Increases Gradually Week by Week 153

According to the Eastern Newspaper, since the beginning of June, due to the sharp drop in silver prices, trade with China has been hit hard, with shipments temporarily decreasing by about two-thirds. Observing the trade between Osaka and Shanghai in terms of volume, it was extremely sluggish in the early and mid-June, with cargo loading only reaching about one-third of normal levels. After mid-month, the Sino-Japanese exchange rate stabilized slightly.

Starting from the 17th and 18th, it gradually increased. For example, the Osaka loading volume of Nippon Yusen ships was only about 500-600 tons per ship before mid-month. The Ikoma Maru, departing on the 18th, carried about 1,100 tons, almost doubling. Subsequently, the Kasagi Maru on the 21st carried 1,000 tons, the Aso Maru on the 25th carried 1,000 tons, and the Tenyo Maru on the 26th carried 1,300 tons. The Yayo Maru, departing at the end of the month, is currently loading, and the numbers are not yet clear, but it is predicted to be about 1,200-1,300 tons. Separated by weeks, it was 1,400 tons in the first week, 3,000 tons in the middle week, and 4,500 tons in the last week, totaling 8,500 tons, gradually increasing week by week, an increase of about 60% compared to the initial forecast of 5,000-6,000 tons. Observing its exports in terms of content, winter cotton fabrics have increased significantly, showing a changing trend in the season. Although silver prices are still soft, trade with China has gradually returned to normal, because the auction items in Japan are currently being shipped to China, and the low silver prices and falling prices of products shipped by ships are enough to offset each other.

Spanish Fabrics Switch to Japanese Silk

Chinese Silk Will Lose a Customer 154

Our country's tea and silk foreign trade is being taken over by the Japanese year by year, and the trend is becoming increasingly sluggish. According to Japanese News, Japanese raw silk has traditionally been sold exclusively to the United States, with only about 10% sold in Europe, showing a declining trend year by year. Recently, the Spanish Baucelo Norway manufacturing company has been using Chinese and French silk. Now, because Japanese silk has durability and the fabrics are strong, it has recently purchased Japanese silk. Thus, Chinese silk will lose another sales channel to Europe.

Tadashi Kametaro Takikawa

Authoring Textual Research on Records of the Grand Historian 155

Making the Study of Records of the Grand Historian a Lifelong Career

The Original Manuscript is Approximately 3,000 Pages

According to Japanese News, Takikawa Kametaro, a professor of Chinese literature at the Second High School in Japan, has now completed the book "Textual Research on Records of the Grand Historian." Mr. Takikawa, who graduated from the Department of Classical Literature at the University of Tokyo, is 65 years old this year. He has been teaching at the Second High School for a long time and has made the study of Records of the Grand Historian his lifelong career. He has come to China to search for reference books. Due to economic difficulties, he has sold books to make ends meet. After many difficulties over 20 years, he has finally completed the book. The original manuscript is approximately 3,000 pages long, and the commentary is all in Chinese. It will take another three years to publish. It is a masterpiece worthy of special mention in the history of Chinese literature research in Japan.
